<p><b>Bogor</b> (<a href="/wiki/Sundanese_language" title="Sundanese language">Sundanese</a>: ᮘᮧᮌᮧᮁ, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i>Buitenzorg</i>) is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cities_of_Indonesia" title="Cities of Indonesia">city</a> in the <a href="/wiki/West_Java" title="West Java">West Java</a> <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Indonesia" title="Provinces of Indonesia">province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>. Located around 60 kilometers (37 mi) south from the national capital of <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>, Bogor is the 6th largest city of <a href="/wiki/Jabodetabek" title="Jabodetabek">Jabodetabek</a> (Jakarta metropolitan region) and the 14th nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kesehat_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-kesehat-3">[3]</a></sup> Bogor is an important economic, scientific, cultural and tourist center, as well as a mountain resort.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, the city served as the capital of <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Kingdom" title="Sunda Kingdom">Sunda Kingdom</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Kerajaan Sunda</i></span>) and was called <i><b>Pakuan Pajajaran</b></i> or <i><b>Dayeuh Pakuan</b></i>. During the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch colonial era</a>, it was named <i><b>Buitenzorg</b></i> (meaning <i>"Without worries"</i> in Dutch) and served as the summer residence of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor-General" title="Governor-General">Governor-General</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>.</p>
<p>With several hundred thousand people living on an area of about 20 km<sup>2</sup> (7.7 sq mi), the central part of Bogor is one of the world's most densely populated areas. The city has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Istana_Bogor" title="Istana Bogor">presidential palace</a> and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bogor_Botanical_Garden" title="Bogor Botanical Garden">botanical garden</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Kebun Raya Bogor</i></span>) – one of the oldest and largest in the world. It bears the nickname "the Rain City" (<i>Kota Hujan</i>), because of frequent rain showers. It nearly always rains even during the dry season.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sunda_Kingdom.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="303" data-file-width="598" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Sunda_Kingdom.svg/220px-Sunda_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Sunda_Kingdom.svg/330px-Sunda_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Sunda_Kingdom.svg/440px-Sunda_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sunda_Kingdom.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Kingdom of Sunda had its capital in Pakuan Pajajaran</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Precolonial_period">Precolonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Precolonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pakuanpajajaran.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="888" data-file-width="980" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Pakuanpajajaran.jpg/220px-Pakuanpajajaran.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Pakuanpajajaran.jpg/330px-Pakuanpajajaran.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Pakuanpajajaran.jpg/440px-Pakuanpajajaran.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pakuanpajajaran.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Dutch map showing the location of the Pakuan Pajajaran relatively to Buitenzorg.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Pakuan_Pajajaran" title="Pakuan Pajajaran">Pakuan Pajajaran</a></div>
<p>The first mentioning of a settlement at present Bogor dates to the 5th century when the area was part of <a href="/wiki/Tarumanagara" title="Tarumanagara">Tarumanagara</a>, one of the earliest states in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indonesian_history" title="Indonesian history">Indonesian history</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Iskandar_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Iskandar-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-History-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15_abad_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-15_abad-6">[6]</a></sup> After a series of defeats from the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">Srivijaya</a>, Tarumanagara was transformed into the <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Kingdom" title="Sunda Kingdom">Sunda Kingdom</a>, and in 669, the capital of Sunda was built between two parallel rivers, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ciliwung" title="Ciliwung">Ciliwung</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cisadane_River" title="Cisadane River">Cisadane</a>. It was named <a href="/wiki/Pakuan_Pajajaran" title="Pakuan Pajajaran">Pakuan Pajajaran</a>, that in old Sundanese means "a place between the parallel [rivers]", and became the predecessor of the modern Bogor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pasundan_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pasundan-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cikalbogor_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-cikalbogor-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prasasti_tugu.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="480" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Prasasti_tugu.jpg/220px-Prasasti_tugu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Prasasti_tugu.jpg/330px-Prasasti_tugu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Prasasti_tugu.jpg/440px-Prasasti_tugu.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prasasti_tugu.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A 1600-year-old stone inscription (<i>prasasti</i>) of the <a href="/wiki/Tarumanagara" title="Tarumanagara">Tarumanagara</a> kingdom era.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Over the next several centuries, Pakuan Pajajaran become one of the largest cities in medieval Indonesia with population reaching 48,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cikalbogor_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-cikalbogor-8">[8]</a></sup> The name Pajajaran was then used for the entire kingdom, and the capital was simply called Pakuan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cikalbogor_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-cikalbogor-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sunda_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-sunda-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cikalbogor2_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-cikalbogor2-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Koler_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Koler-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karta_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Karta-12">[12]</a></sup> The chronicles of that time were written in <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a>, which was the language used for official and religious purposes, using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pallava" title="Pallava">Pallava</a> writing system, on rock stellas called prasasti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-History-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prasasti_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-prasasti-13">[13]</a></sup> The prasasti found in and around Bogor differ in shape and text style from other Indonesian prasasti and are among the main attractions of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-History-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 9–15th centuries, the capital was moving between Pakuan and other cities of the kingdom, and finally returned to Pakuan by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Siliwangi" title="King Siliwangi">King Siliwangi</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Sri_Baduga_Maharaja" title="Sri Baduga Maharaja">Sri Baduga Maharaja</a></i>) on 3 June 1482 – the day of his coronation. Since 1973, this date is celebrated in Bogor as an official city holiday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o144_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-o144-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-depok_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-depok-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1579, Pakuan was captured and almost completely destroyed by the army of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Banten" title="Sultanate of Banten">Sultanate of Banten</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VI_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-VI-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bolshaya_Soviet_entsiklopediya2_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bolshaya_Soviet_entsiklopediya2-17">[17]</a></sup> ceasing the existence of the State of Sunda. The city was abandoned and remained uninhabited for decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cikalbogor_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-cikalbogor-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o144_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-o144-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period">Colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_East_India_Company">Dutch East India Company</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Dutch East India Company">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the second half of the 17th century, the abandoned Pakuan as most of West Java, while formally remaining under the Sultanate of Banten, gradually passed under control of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> (VOC). The formal transition occurred on 17 April 1684 by signing an agreement between the Crown Prince of Banten and the VOC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-depok2_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-depok2-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first, and temporal, colonial settlement at Pakuan was a camp of lieutenant Tanoejiwa, a <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> employed by the VOC who was sent in 1687 to develop the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cikalbogor2_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-cikalbogor2-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-depok2_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-depok2-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup> It was seriously damaged by the eruption on 4–5 January 1699 of the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Salak" title="Mount Salak">Mount Salak</a> volcano (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Gunung Salak</i></span>), however the concomitant forest fires removed much forest, leaving much area for the planned rice and coffee plantations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cikalbogor2_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-cikalbogor2-10">[10]</a></sup> In a short time, several agricultural settlements appeared around Pakuan, the largest being Kampung Baru (lit. "new village").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-History-5">[5]</a></sup> In 1701, they were combined into an administrative district; Tanoejiwa was chosen as the head of the district and is regarded as the founder of the modern <a href="/wiki/Bogor_Regency" title="Bogor Regency">Bogor Regency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-depok2_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-depok2-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The district was further developed during the 1703 Dutch mission headed by the Inspector General of the VOC <a href="/wiki/Abraham_van_Riebeeck" title="Abraham van Riebeeck">Abraham van Riebeeck</a> (the son of the founder of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a> <a href="/wiki/Jan_van_Riebeeck" title="Jan van Riebeeck">Jan van Riebeeck</a> and later Governor of Dutch East Indies).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cikalbogor2_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-cikalbogor2-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-depok2_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-depok2-18">[18]</a></sup> The expedition of van Riebeeck performed a detailed study of the Pakuan ruins, discovered and described many archaeological artifacts, including prasasti, and erected buildings for the VOC employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup> The area attracted the Dutch by a favorable geographical position and mild climate, preferred over the hot <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Batavia</a> which was then the administrative center of the Dutch East Indies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-3"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup> In 1744–1745, the residence of the Governor-General was built in Pakuan which was hosting the government during the summer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-4"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Olieverfschildering_voorstellend_de_grote_postweg_bij_Buitenzorg_TMnr_1012-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="525" data-file-width="800" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Olieverfschildering_voorstellend_de_grote_postweg_bij_Buitenzorg_TMnr_1012-1.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Olieverfschildering_voorstellend_de_grote_postweg_bij_Buitenzorg_TMnr_1012-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Olieverfschildering_voorstellend_de_grote_postweg_bij_Buitenzorg_TMnr_1012-1.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Olieverfschildering_voorstellend_de_grote_postweg_bij_Buitenzorg_TMnr_1012-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Olieverfschildering_voorstellend_de_grote_postweg_bij_Buitenzorg_TMnr_1012-1.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Olieverfschildering_voorstellend_de_grote_postweg_bij_Buitenzorg_TMnr_1012-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Olieverfschildering_voorstellend_de_grote_postweg_bij_Buitenzorg_TMnr_1012-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Great_Post_Road" title="Great Post Road">Great Post Road</a> passing Buitenzorg in the 19th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1746, by the order of the Governor-General <a href="/wiki/Gustaaf_Willem_van_Imhoff" title="Gustaaf Willem van Imhoff">Gustaaf Willem van Imhoff</a>, the Palace, a nearby Dutch settlement and nine native settlements were merged into an administrative division named Buitenzorg (Dutch for "beyond (or outside) concerns," meaning "without worries" or "carefree," cf. Frederick the Great of Prussia's summer palace outside Potsdam, Sanssouci, with the same meaning in French.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica1911_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica1911-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unof_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-unof-21">[21]</a></sup> Around the same time, the first reference to <i>Bogor</i> as the local name of the city was documented; it was mentioned in the administration report from 7 April 1752 with respect to the part of Buitenzorg adjacent to the Palace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pasundanskaya_istoriya_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pasundanskaya_istoriya-22">[22]</a></sup> Later this name became used for the whole city as the local alternative to Buitenzorg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica1911_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica1911-20">[20]</a></sup> This name is believed to originate from the Javanese word <i>bogor</i> meaning sugar palm (<i>Arenga pinnata</i>), which is still used in the Indonesian language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pasundanskaya_istoriya_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pasundanskaya_istoriya-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KBBI_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-KBBI-23">[23]</a></sup> Alternative origins are the old-Javanese word <i>bhagar</i> (meaning cow), or simply the misspelling of "Buitenzorg" by the local residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pasundanskaya_istoriya_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-Pasundanskaya_istoriya-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city grew rapidly in the late 18th – early 19th centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-5"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup> This growth was partly stimulated by the temporary occupation of the Dutch East Indies by United Kingdom in 1811–1815 – the British landed on Java and other <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Islands" title="Sunda Islands">Sunda Islands</a> to prevent their capture by <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">Napoleonic France</a> which then conquered the Netherlands. The head of the British administration <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Raffles" title="Stamford Raffles">Stamford Raffles</a> moved the administrative center from Batavia to Buitenzorg and implemented new and more efficient management techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-6"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raffles_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Raffles-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rule_of_the_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands">Rule of the Kingdom of the Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Rule of the Kingdom of the Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_%27s_Lands_Plantentuin_te_Buitenzorg._TMnr_60012830.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="700" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_%27s_Lands_Plantentuin_te_Buitenzorg._TMnr_60012830.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_%27s_Lands_Plantentuin_te_Buitenzorg._TMnr_60012830.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_%27s_Lands_Plantentuin_te_Buitenzorg._TMnr_60012830.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_%27s_Lands_Plantentuin_te_Buitenzorg._TMnr_60012830.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_%27s_Lands_Plantentuin_te_Buitenzorg._TMnr_60012830.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_%27s_Lands_Plantentuin_te_Buitenzorg._TMnr_60012830.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_%27s_Lands_Plantentuin_te_Buitenzorg._TMnr_60012830.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bogor Palace in 1910s when it was still the residence of Governor-General.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After Buitenzorg was returned to the Dutch, it fell under the rule of the Kingdom of the Netherlands rather than VOC. The Buitenzorg Palace was reinstated as the summer residence of the Governor-General. A botanical garden was set up nearby in 1817, which was one of the world's largest gardens in the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-7"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica1911_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica1911-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GE_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-GE-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Buitenzorg_(Baedeker,_1914).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1508" data-file-width="983" height="337" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Map_of_Buitenzorg_%28Baedeker%2C_1914%29.jpg/220px-Map_of_Buitenzorg_%28Baedeker%2C_1914%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Map_of_Buitenzorg_%28Baedeker%2C_1914%29.jpg/330px-Map_of_Buitenzorg_%28Baedeker%2C_1914%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Map_of_Buitenzorg_%28Baedeker%2C_1914%29.jpg/440px-Map_of_Buitenzorg_%28Baedeker%2C_1914%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Buitenzorg_(Baedeker,_1914).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Baedeker" title="Baedeker">Baedeker</a> map of the town, ca 1914</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 10 October 1834, Buitenzorg was seriously damaged by another eruption of the Salak volcanoes caused by an earthquake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-8"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JP_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-JP-27">[27]</a></sup> Taking into account the seismic activity of the region, the governor's palace and office buildings constructed in 1840–1850 were built shorter but sturdier than those built prior to the eruption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-9"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup> The Governor's decree of 1845 prescribed separate settlements of European, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Han_(people)" title="Han (people)">Chinese</a> and Arab migrants within the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-10"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1860–1880, the largest agricultural school in the colony was established in Buitenzorg. Other scientific institutions including a city library, natural science museum, biology, chemistry, and veterinary medicine laboratories were also constructed during this period. By the end of the 19th century, Buitenzorg became one of the most developed and Westernized cities in Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cikalbogor2_10-4"><a href="#cite_note-cikalbogor2-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-11"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1904, Buitenzorg formally became the administrative center of the Dutch East Indies. However, real management remained in Batavia, which hosted most of the administrative offices and the main office of the governor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-History-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica1911_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica1911-20">[20]</a></sup> This status was revoked in the administrative reform of 1924, which divided the colony into provinces and set Buitenzorg as the center of West Java Province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-History-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="1942–1950"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1942.E2.80.931950">1942–1950</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1942–1950">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Luchtfoto_van_het_paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60027049.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="486" data-file-width="700" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Luchtfoto_van_het_paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60027049.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Luchtfoto_van_het_paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60027049.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Luchtfoto_van_het_paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60027049.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Luchtfoto_van_het_paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60027049.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Luchtfoto_van_het_paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60027049.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Luchtfoto_van_het_paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60027049.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Luchtfoto_van_het_paleis_van_de_Gouverneur-Generaal_in_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60027049.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial picture of Bogor during the 1930s.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Het_hoofd_van_de_deelstaat_Negara_Pasundan_met_zijn_secretaris_TMnr_60054594.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="495" data-file-width="700" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Het_hoofd_van_de_deelstaat_Negara_Pasundan_met_zijn_secretaris_TMnr_60054594.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Het_hoofd_van_de_deelstaat_Negara_Pasundan_met_zijn_secretaris_TMnr_60054594.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Het_hoofd_van_de_deelstaat_Negara_Pasundan_met_zijn_secretaris_TMnr_60054594.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Het_hoofd_van_de_deelstaat_Negara_Pasundan_met_zijn_secretaris_TMnr_60054594.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Het_hoofd_van_de_deelstaat_Negara_Pasundan_met_zijn_secretaris_TMnr_60054594.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Het_hoofd_van_de_deelstaat_Negara_Pasundan_met_zijn_secretaris_TMnr_60054594.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Het_hoofd_van_de_deelstaat_Negara_Pasundan_met_zijn_secretaris_TMnr_60054594.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
R. A. A. Muharram <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Wiranatakusuma&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Wiranatakusuma (page does not exist)">Wiranatakusuma</a>, president of the Pasundan State with his secretary in Bogor (1948)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Buitenzorg and the entire territory of Dutch East Indies were occupied by Japanese forces; the occupation lasted from 6 March 1942 until the summer of 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Japanese_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Japanese-28">[28]</a></sup> As part of the efforts by the Japanese to promote nationalist (and thus anti-Dutch) sentiments among the local population the city was given the Indonesian name Bogor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GE_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-GE-26">[26]</a></sup> The city had one of the major training centres of the Indonesian militia PETA (Pembela Tanah Air – "<i>Defenders of the Motherland</i>").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PETA_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-PETA-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 August 1945, Soekarno and Hatta proclaimed independence, but the Dutch regained control of the town and adjoining areas. In February 1948, Buitenzorg was included in the quasi-independent state of West Java,(<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Negara Jawa Barat</i></span>) which was renamed <a href="/wiki/Pasundan" title="Pasundan">Pasundan</a> in April 1948 (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Negara Pasundan</i></span>). This state was established by the Netherlands as a step to transform their former colonial possessions in the East Indies into a dependent federation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pasundan..._30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pasundan...-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VI12_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-VI12-31">[31]</a></sup> In December 1949, Pasundan joined the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_United_States_of_Indonesia" title="Republic of the United States of Indonesia">Republic of the United States of Indonesia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Republik Indonesia Serikat</i></span>, RIS) established at the <a href="/wiki/Dutch%E2%80%93Indonesian_Round_Table_Conference" title="Dutch–Indonesian Round Table Conference">Dutch–Indonesian Round Table Conference</a> of 23 August – 2 November 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VI12_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-VI12-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-II_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-II-32">[32]</a></sup> In February 1950, as a result of defeat of Pasundan in a quick military conflict with the Republic of Indonesia, the city became part of Indonesia, as formalized in August 1950,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VI12_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-VI12-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-II_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-II-32">[32]</a></sup> and its name was officially declared as Bogor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o144_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-o144-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UU16-50_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-UU16-50-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="As_part_of_Indonesia">As part of Indonesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: As part of Indonesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As part of independent Indonesia, Bogor has a significant role in the cultural, scientific and economic development of the country and West Java in particular – in part due to the legacy of infrastructure built during the colonial period. Its special position was further reinforced by the transformation of the former summer residence of the governor-general into the summer palace of the President of Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cikalbogor2_10-5"><a href="#cite_note-cikalbogor2-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Istana_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Istana-34">[34]</a></sup> In the 1990s–2000s, the city regularly hosted various international events, such as ministry-level meetings of the Asia-Pacific institutions<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Klimat_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Klimat-35">[35]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">APEC</a> summit of 15 November 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATES_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-ATES-36">[36]</a></sup> Since 2008, a Christian church congregation in Bogor has been embroiled with <a href="/wiki/Islamic_fundamentalism" title="Islamic fundamentalism">Islamic fundamentalists</a> over the building permit for their new church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="Geography,_topography,_geology"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography.2C_topography.2C_geology">Geography, topography, geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography, topography, geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ciliwung_090419-7685.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="800" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Ciliwung_090419-7685.JPG/220px-Ciliwung_090419-7685.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Ciliwung_090419-7685.JPG/330px-Ciliwung_090419-7685.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Ciliwung_090419-7685.JPG/440px-Ciliwung_090419-7685.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ciliwung_090419-7685.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ciliwung_River" title="Ciliwung River">Ciliwung River</a> on the outskirts of Bogor</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kota_Bogor_%26_Gunung_Salak.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Kota_Bogor_%26_Gunung_Salak.jpg/220px-Kota_Bogor_%26_Gunung_Salak.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Kota_Bogor_%26_Gunung_Salak.jpg/330px-Kota_Bogor_%26_Gunung_Salak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Kota_Bogor_%26_Gunung_Salak.jpg/440px-Kota_Bogor_%26_Gunung_Salak.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kota_Bogor_%26_Gunung_Salak.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bogor and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Salak" title="Mount Salak">Mount Salak</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city is situated in the western part of <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> island, about 53 km south of the capital <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a> and 85 km northwest of <a href="/wiki/Bandung" title="Bandung">Bandung</a>, the administrative center of West Java Province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o148_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-o148-1">[1]</a></sup> Bogor spreads over a <a href="/wiki/Structural_basin" title="Structural basin">basin</a> near volcanoes Salak, which peaks at about 12 km south, and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Gede" title="Mount Gede">Mount Gede</a> whose top is 22–25 km south-east of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o691_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-o691-38">[38]</a></sup> The average elevation is 265 meters, maximum 330 m, and minimum 190 meters above sea level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o148_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-o148-1">[1]</a></sup> The terrain is rather uneven: 17.64 km² of its area has slopes of 0–2°, 80.9 km² from 2° to 15°, 11 km² between 15° and 25°, 7.65 km² from 25° to 40° and 1.20 km² over 40°;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o771-5_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-o771-5-39">[39]</a></sup> the northern part is relatively flat and the southern part is more hilly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o771-6_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-o771-6-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The soils are dominated by volcanic sedimentary rocks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o771-6_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-o771-6-40">[40]</a></sup> Given the proximity of large active volcanoes, the area is considered highly seismic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o691_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-o691-38">[38]</a></sup> The total area of green space is 205,000 m², of which 87,000 m² are <a href="/wiki/Bogor_Botanical_Gardens" title="Bogor Botanical Gardens">Bogor Botanical Gardens</a>, 19,400 m² are taken by 35 parks, 17,200 m² by 24 groves and 81,400 m² are covered with grass.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hijau_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hijau-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several rivers flow through the city toward the <a href="/wiki/Java_Sea" title="Java Sea">Java Sea</a>. The largest ones, Ciliwung and Cisadane, flank the historic city center. Smaller rivers, Cipakancilan, Cidepit, Ciparigi and Cibalok, are guided by cement tubes in many places.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o691_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-o691-38">[38]</a></sup> It is worth noting that "ci" in the river names merely means "river" in Sundanese, and the actual name begins after it, but the "ci" is nevertheless included into national and international maps. There are several small lakes within the city, including Situ Burung (lit. Bird Lake; "Situ" meaning "Lake") and Situ Gede (lit. Great Lake), with the area of several hectares each. Rivers and lakes occupy 2.89% of the city area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o694-3_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-o694-3-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bogor has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">tropical rainforest climate</a> (Af) according to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClimateData.org_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-ClimateData.org-43">[43]</a></sup> and more humid and rainy than in many other areas of West Java – the average <a href="/wiki/Relative_humidity" title="Relative humidity">relative humidity</a> is 70%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o691_38-3"><a href="#cite_note-o691-38">[38]</a></sup> the average annual precipitation is about 1700 mm, but more than 3500 mm in some areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o691_38-4"><a href="#cite_note-o691-38">[38]</a></sup> Most rain falls between December and February. Because of this weather, Bogor has the nickname "Rain City" (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Kota hujan</i></span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bogor_Raya_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bogor_Raya-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kota_Hujan_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kota_Hujan-45">[45]</a></sup> The temperatures are lower than in coastal Java: the average maximum is 25.9 °C (cf. 32.2 °C in Jakarta). Daily fluctuations (9–10 °C) are rather high for Indonesia. The absolute maximum temperature was recorded at 38 °C and the minimum at 3 °C.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o148_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-o148-1">[1]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The New American Cyclopaedia of 1867 reported Buitenzorg's population as being 320,756 including 9,530 Chinese, 650 Europeans, and 23 Arabs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the national census held in May–August 2010, 949,066 people were registered in Bogor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sensus_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sensus-47">[47]</a></sup> The average population density is about 8,000 people per km²; it reaches 12,571 persons per km² in the centre and drops to 5,866 people per km² in the southern part.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sensus_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sensus-47">[47]</a></sup> Based on BPS data,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPS_Population_Data_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-BPS_Population_Data-2">[2]</a></sup> Bogor population in 2014 was 1,030,720 people, suggesting a population density of 8,698 people/km<sup>2</sup>.</p>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta,_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1180" data-file-width="1575" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta%2C_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg/220px-Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta%2C_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta%2C_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg/330px-Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta%2C_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta%2C_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg/440px-Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta%2C_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkartta,_Candi_Siliwangi_Shrine.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> shrine dedicated to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Siliwangi" title="King Siliwangi">King Siliwangi</a>, in the Hindu temple <a href="/wiki/Pura_Parahyangan_Agung_Jagatkarta" title="Pura Parahyangan Agung Jagatkarta">Pura Parahyangan Agung Jagatkarta</a>, the second largest temple in Indonesia. Pakuan Pajajaran (Bogor) is the capital region of the Sunda <a href="/wiki/Galuh_Kingdom" title="Galuh Kingdom">Galuh Kingdom</a>, the last Hindu kingdom in the archipelago along with <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahit</a>.</div>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Women_in_KRB.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Women_in_KRB.JPG/220px-Women_in_KRB.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Women_in_KRB.JPG/330px-Women_in_KRB.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Women_in_KRB.JPG/440px-Women_in_KRB.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

School girls in Muslim dress in the Bogor Botanical Garden</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The rapid population growth in Bogor after 1960 is related to urbanization as well as the influx of workforce from other parts of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Demografiya_50-4"><a href="#cite_note-Demografiya-50">[50]</a></sup> The birth rate in 2009 was 563 children per 10,000 people, with the mortality value of 272. During the same year, 12,709 permanent resident moved in and 3,391 people left the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistika_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Statistika-51">[51]</a></sup> Men constituted 51.06% and women 48.94% of the population;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sensus_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-Sensus-47">[47]</a></sup> 28.39% of the inhabitants were under 15 years old, 67.42% were aged 15–65 years and 3.51% – over 65 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistika_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Statistika-51">[51]</a></sup> The 2005 estimate of the <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> is 71.8 years, which is the highest figure for West Java and one of the highest in Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHH_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-AHH-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most population (87%) are <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a>, with considerable numbers of <a href="/wiki/Betawi_people" title="Betawi people">Betawi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a>, Chinese and other, often mixed ethnicities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPNS_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-CPNS-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HUT528_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-HUT528-54">[54]</a></sup> Virtually all adults are fluent in <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a> – the official language of the country. <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_language" title="Sundanese language">Sundanese</a> is used at home and in some public areas and events – for example, the solemn speech of the mayor at the City Day celebration of 3 June 2010 was delivered in Sundanese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HUT528_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-HUT528-54">[54]</a></sup> The local <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialect</a> of Sundanese significantly differs from the classical version both lexically and phonetically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dialect_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-dialect-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dialect2_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-dialect2-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>The majority of population (94%) are <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agama_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-agama-57">[57]</a></sup> with just over 5% Christians. However, there are many Christian churches in the city,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kristen_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-kristen-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kristen2_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-kristen2-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kristen3_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-kristen3-60">[60]</a></sup> as well as Buddhist (mostly in the Chinese community<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bud_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-bud-61">[61]</a></sup>) and Hindu communities.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bogor City is surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Bogor_Regency" title="Bogor Regency">Bogor Regency</a> (<a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Indonesia" title="Provinces of Indonesia"><i>kabupaten</i></a>) but in itself is a separate municipality (<a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Indonesia" title="Provinces of Indonesia"><i>cat</i></a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o144_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-o144-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UU32-2004_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-UU32-2004-62">[62]</a></sup> The city is divided into six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Districts_of_Indonesia" title="Districts of Indonesia">districts</a> (<i>kecamatan</i>), which contain 68 low-level administrative units, 31 of which have the status of settlement and 37 are villages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o767_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-o767-63">[63]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city is headed by a mayor, who is elected by the citizens every five years, together with a vice-mayor; in the past, the mayor was appointed by the provincial administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UU32-2004_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-UU32-2004-62">[62]</a></sup> Diani Budiarto became the first elected mayor of Bogor on 25 October 2008 and assumed his position on 7 April 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o484_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-o484-64">[64]</a></sup> Legislative power is provided by the City Council which consists of 45 people's representatives who are also elected by the residents for a 5-year term. Nine political parties consisting of five <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_group" title="Parliamentary group">factions</a> are represented in the Council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o644_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-o644-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o644-2_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-o644-2-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The coat of arms of Bogor is a rectangular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heraldic_shield" title="Heraldic shield">heraldic shield</a> with a pointed base and the side lengths ratio of 5:4, divided by a cross into four parts. The upper left quarter contains the <a href="/wiki/National_emblem" title="National emblem">National</a> <a href="/wiki/National_emblem_of_Indonesia" title="National emblem of Indonesia">Emblem of Indonesia</a> – the mythical bird <a href="/wiki/Garuda" title="Garuda">Garuda</a>, in the upper right is the presidential palace, in the bottom left is the Salak volcano, and in the lower right is the national Sundanese <a href="/wiki/Dagger" title="Dagger">dagger</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Kujang_(weapon)" title="Kujang (weapon)">kujang</a></i>. The inscription on top reads "KOTA BOGOR" which translates to "THE CITY OF BOGOR".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o146_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-o146-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bogor_street-2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Bogor_street-2.JPG/220px-Bogor_street-2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Bogor_street-2.JPG/330px-Bogor_street-2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Bogor_street-2.JPG/440px-Bogor_street-2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bogor_street-2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A building in downtown Bogor</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Poecilia_retic_090519-8649_kdBdk.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1148" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Poecilia_retic_090519-8649_kdBdk.jpg/220px-Poecilia_retic_090519-8649_kdBdk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Poecilia_retic_090519-8649_kdBdk.jpg/330px-Poecilia_retic_090519-8649_kdBdk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Poecilia_retic_090519-8649_kdBdk.jpg/440px-Poecilia_retic_090519-8649_kdBdk.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Poecilia_retic_090519-8649_kdBdk.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Guppy" title="Guppy">Guppy</a> fishes are exported in large quantities from Bogor.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bogor has developed <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry" title="Automotive industry">automotive</a> <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemical</a> and food industries;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o693_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-o693-68">[68]</a></sup> its outlying areas are used for agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPPT-Pertanian_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-BPPT-Pertanian-69">[69]</a></sup> During the colonization, Bogor was mostly producing coffee, rubber and high-quality timber. Chemical industry was introduced to the city at the end of the 19th century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cikalbogor2_10-6"><a href="#cite_note-cikalbogor2-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-12"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup> and car and metal production in the 1950s, during the industrialization of independent Indonesia. The fast economic development of the 1980s was slowed down by the crisis of the 1990s and recovered in the early 2000s; so the growth rate of the economy in Bogor was 5.78% in 2002, 6.07% in 2003 and 6.02% in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o693_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-o693-68">[68]</a></sup> At the end of 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Gross_Regional_Product" title="Gross Regional Product">Gross Regional Product</a> (GRP) was 12.249 trillion <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indonesian_Rupiah" title="Indonesian Rupiah">IDR</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Svezhie_ekonomdannye_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Svezhie_ekonomdannye-70">[70]</a></sup> (approximately 1.287 billion USD<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-exchange_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-exchange-71">[71]</a></sup>) and the investments amounted to 932.295 billion IDR.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Svezhie_ekonomdannye_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-Svezhie_ekonomdannye-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the economical growth, the number of citizens living below the poverty level (defined by not only cash income, but also access to basic social services<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o771-20_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-o771-20-72">[72]</a></sup>) is increasing, primarily due to the inflow of poor residents of the surrounding rural areas. In 2009, 17.45% of the population lived below the poverty level, almost twice higher than in 2006 (9.5%)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Svezhie_ekonomdannye_70-2"><a href="#cite_note-Svezhie_ekonomdannye-70">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">Minimum wage</a> is established by the West Java Governor at 2,658,155 IDR/month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>

</tr>

<td>30.14</td>
</tr>

<p>In 2008 there were 3,208 officially registered industrial enterprises in Bogor employing 54,268 people, more than half (32,237) of whom worked at the 114 largest companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPPT-Industri_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-BPPT-Industri-75">[75]</a></sup> The outskirts of the city contain about 3,466 hectares of agricultural area, including 111 hectares of water bodies used for fishery and fish farming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPPT-Pertanian_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-BPPT-Pertanian-69">[69]</a></sup> The main crops are rice (1165 hectares as of 2007, the annual harvest in 2003 was 9,953 tonnes), various vegetables (772 acres, 8,296 tonnes), corn (382 acres, 6,720 tonnes) and <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potato</a> (480 acres, 3,480 tonnes).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Urozhay_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Urozhay-76">[76]</a></sup> The livestock sector has 25 registered companies (as of 2007) mostly breeding cows (more than 1000 animals yielding more than 2.61 million liters of milk), sheep (about 12,000), chickens (more than 642,000) and ducks (ca. 8,000).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o771-15_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-o771-15-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o771-16_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-o771-16-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>About 25–30 tonnes of various species of fish are produced per year by 4 registered companies. The fishes are mostly bred artificially, in ponds and paddy fields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o771-17_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-o771-17-79">[79]</a></sup> Breeding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aquarium_fish" title="Aquarium fish">aquarium fish</a> and also catching them in their natural habitat is an important industry sector, which yielded 367,000 USD from 2008 export sales only, mostly to Japan and Middle East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ade_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ade-74">[74]</a></sup> A substantial part of other Bogor production, 144 billion IDR in 2008, is exported. Examples are clothes and footwear (to US, EU, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations_East_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations East Asia (page does not exist)">ASEAN</a>, Canada, Australia, Russia), textiles (US, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>), furniture (South Korea), car tires (ASEAN countries and South America), toys and souvenirs (Japan, Germany, Brazil), soft drinks (ASEAN countries and Middle East).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPPT-Perdagangan_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-BPPT-Perdagangan-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o698_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-o698-81">[81]</a></sup> Most of the local sells are carried out via the eight major shopping centers, nine supermarkets and seven major markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPPT-Perdagangan_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-BPPT-Perdagangan-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bogor_Station.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="591" data-file-width="1024" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Bogor_Station.jpg/220px-Bogor_Station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Bogor_Station.jpg/330px-Bogor_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Bogor_Station.jpg/440px-Bogor_Station.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bogor_Station.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bogor railway station</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Becak_Bogor.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1536" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Becak_Bogor.jpg/220px-Becak_Bogor.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Becak_Bogor.jpg/330px-Becak_Bogor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Becak_Bogor.jpg/440px-Becak_Bogor.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Becak_Bogor.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Becak parking at the center of Bogor</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bogor is a major transport center of Java. It contains 599.2 kilometers of roads (as of 2008) which cover 5.31% of the city area; 30.2 kilometers of the roads are of national and 26.8 km of prefectural importance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPPT-Prasarana_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-BPPT-Prasarana-82">[82]</a></sup> The 22 transport lines are operated by 3,506 buses and minibuses. In addition, 10 bus routes connect the city with the nearest metropolitan area (4,612 buses) and 40 with other cities of West Java (330 buses).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o151-8_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-o151-8-83">[83]</a></sup> There are two major bus terminals, Baranangsiang and Bubulak. The former has an area of 22,100 m² and is dedicated to long-distance and freight traffic while the latter (area 11,850 m²) serves urban passenger routes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o151-9_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-o151-9-84">[84]</a></sup> A separate station is dedicated to tourist coaches and buses to the nearest <a href="/wiki/Soekarno%E2%80%93Hatta_International_Airport" title="Soekarno–Hatta International Airport">Soekarno–Hatta International Airport</a> in Jakarta, located about 55 kilometers from Bogor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o151-9_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-o151-9-84">[84]</a></sup> Recent years see a significant increase in the number of traditional Indonesian <a href="/wiki/Cycle_rickshaw" title="Cycle rickshaw">rickshaw</a> (<i>becak</i>) at more than 2,000 units as of 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-becak_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-becak-85">[85]</a></sup> The train station of Bogor was built in 1881, and currently serves about 50,000 passengers and has about 70 departures and 70 arrivals per day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o151-9_84-2"><a href="#cite_note-o151-9-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing_and_facilities">Housing and facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Housing and facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Residential buildings occupy 26.46% of the city, or 71.11% of its built-up area; 5–14-storey buildings dominate the central part and the outlying areas are mostly built up with single-storeyed houses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSS_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-RSS-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bappeda_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bappeda-87">[87]</a></sup> The population rise in the 1990s–2000s due to the inflow of external workforce sharply increased the number of substandard housing, mainly on the outskirts of the city. More than half of the slums (1,242,490 m²) are located in northern Bogor, whereas their area is only 89,780 m² in southern part of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bappeda_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bappeda-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kumuh_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kumuh-88">[88]</a></sup> To improve this situation, the city administration launched a program of construction of cheap housing types (light prefabricated houses) in the western Bogor. These houses combine reasonable rent ($22 per year<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Svezhy_kurs_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Svezhy_kurs-89">[89]</a></sup>) at acceptable living conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSS_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-RSS-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Electricity to Bogor is supplied by Indonesian state company Perusahaan Listrik Negara, which serves the provinces of West Java and <a href="/wiki/Banten" title="Banten">Banten</a>. Electricity is provided by more than ten regional thermal and hydroelectric power plants via two local transformer stations located in the Bogor districts of Cimahpar and Cibilong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PLN_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-PLN-90">[90]</a></sup> Whereas most of the houses (excluding some slum areas) are provided with electricity, street lighting covers only 35.38% of the city (4,193 light sources, as of 2007), however, the number of street lights is increasing at an annual rate of 10–15%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lampu_Jalan_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lampu_Jalan-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2009, only 47% of Bogor is provided with clean tap water through a centralized water supply systems managed by state-owned Tirta Pakuan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PDAM_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-PDAM-92">[92]</a></sup> The municipal system takes water from rivers Cisadane (1240 liters per second), and three natural sources: Kota Batu, Bentar-Kambing and Tangka (410 liters per second). Although, the water network has a total length of 741 kilometers and covers about 70% of the city, connection to it is often problematic for financial and technical reasons. More than half of residents use water wells or natural reservoirs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PDAM_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-PDAM-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>Garbage collection service covers 67% of the urban area. From about 800,000 m<sup>3</sup> of waste per year, about 90% is buried at an external landfill at Galuga, about 7% is recycled for <a href="/wiki/Compost" title="Compost">compost</a> and about 3% is burned in five incinerators within the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sampah_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sampah-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>The seven cemeteries of Bogor are named by the city districts as Cilendek, Kayumanis, Situgede, Mulyaharja, Blender, Dreded and Gunung Gadung. The first six have the status of "public cemeteries" (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Tempat pemakaman umum</i></span>), and have no restrictions by religion or ethnicity. However, given the religious composition of Bogor, the cemeteries are predominantly Muslim, and Christian graves are located either in separate areas of cemeteries or in a small cemetery adjacent to churches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TPU_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-TPU-94">[94]</a></sup> Some mosques also have small burial plots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Falak_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Falak-95">[95]</a></sup> Graves for poor and nameless are mostly located at Kayumanis,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bezymyannye_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-bezymyannye-96">[96]</a></sup> and Gunung Gadung cemetery is restricted to Chinese residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pogrom_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-pogrom-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_science">Education and science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Education and science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bogor is one of the major scientific and educational centers in Indonesia. A significant part of academic and research base was laid in the period of Dutch colonization. In particular, since the beginning of the 19th century there were established laboratories and professional schools focused primarily on improving the efficiency of the colonial agricultural;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cikalbogor2_10-7"><a href="#cite_note-cikalbogor2-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theyo_19-13"><a href="#cite_note-theyo-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica1911_20-4"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica1911-20">[20]</a></sup> In the late 19th – early 20th centuries have been established over major scientific institutions – the Research Institute and Rubber Research Institute of Forest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kauchuk_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kauchuk-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Les_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Les-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>Similar to the prevailing profile of research and academic activity was retained in Bogor Indonesia and after gaining independence. As in the second half of 20th century, and in the 2000s strongest areas were agricultural science, <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">Biology</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veterinary" title="Veterinary">Veterinary</a>. The main educational and scientific center with the utmost national importance, is <a href="/wiki/Bogor_Agricultural_University" title="Bogor Agricultural University">Bogor Agricultural University</a>, which structure, in addition to educational facilities, includes dozens of research centers and laboratories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPB_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-IPB-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o764_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-o764-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bogor hosts the global headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_International_Forestry_Research" title="Center for International Forestry Research">Center for International Forestry Research</a> (CIFOR), an international organization conducting research on forestry and human development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIFOR_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIFOR-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CGIAR_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-CGIAR-103">[103]</a></sup> The headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_the_Preservation_of_Birds_and_their_Habitat" title="Organisation for the Preservation of Birds and their Habitat">Organisation for the Preservation of Birds and their Habitat</a> are also in Bogor.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Veeartsenijkundig_laboratorium_te_Buitenzorg_paard_in_de_bascule%27_TMnr_10013160.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="505" data-file-width="700" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Veeartsenijkundig_laboratorium_te_Buitenzorg_paard_in_de_bascule%27_TMnr_10013160.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Veeartsenijkundig_laboratorium_te_Buitenzorg_paard_in_de_bascule%27_TMnr_10013160.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Veeartsenijkundig_laboratorium_te_Buitenzorg_paard_in_de_bascule%27_TMnr_10013160.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Veeartsenijkundig_laboratorium_te_Buitenzorg_paard_in_de_bascule%27_TMnr_10013160.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Veeartsenijkundig_laboratorium_te_Buitenzorg_paard_in_de_bascule%27_TMnr_10013160.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Veeartsenijkundig_laboratorium_te_Buitenzorg_paard_in_de_bascule%27_TMnr_10013160.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Veeartsenijkundig_laboratorium_te_Buitenzorg_paard_in_de_bascule%27_TMnr_10013160.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

</div>
