<p>The literacy rate in Bogor (98.7%) is rather high for Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistika_51-4"><a href="#cite_note-Statistika-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bogor_Agricultural_University" title="Bogor Agricultural University">Bogor Agricultural University</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Institut Pertanian Bogor</i></span>) is the main agricultural university of the country. It was founded in 1963 based on the agricultural college, which was established back in the 19th century by the Dutch colonial administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPB_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-IPB-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vuzy_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-vuzy-104">[104]</a></sup> The largest private universities are Pakuan, Juanda, Nusa Bangsa and Ibn Khaldun.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vuzy_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-vuzy-104">[104]</a></sup> In addition to regular schools, there are over 700 Muslim schools (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madrasah" title="Madrasah">madrasah</a>) and several Christian schools and colleges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistika_51-5"><a href="#cite_note-Statistika-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most scientific research in Bogor is carried out in agriculture, soil science, <a href="/wiki/Dendrology" title="Dendrology">dendrology</a>, veterinary and <a href="/wiki/Ichthyology" title="Ichthyology">ichthyology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPB_100-2"><a href="#cite_note-IPB-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o764_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-o764-101">[101]</a></sup> More specific areas include natural <a href="/wiki/Pesticide" title="Pesticide">pesticides</a> and <a href="/wiki/Insect_repellent" title="Insect repellent">repellents</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intercropping" title="Intercropping">intercropping</a>, industrial applications of <a href="/wiki/Essential_oil" title="Essential oil">essential oils</a> and natural <a href="/wiki/Alkaloid" title="Alkaloid">alkaloids</a>, increasing yields of various kinds of pepper, improving preservation processes, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rabotayut_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-rabotayut-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bogor is one of the leading cities of Indonesia by the number of museums, some of which are among the oldest and largest in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kultura_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-kultura-106">[106]</a></sup> The Zoological Museum (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Museum Zoologi</i></span>) which was opened in 1894 by the Dutch colonial administration as an adjunct to the Botanic Gardens and contains thousands of exhibits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zoo_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-zoo-107">[107]</a></sup> Other prominent musea are more recent. So the museum of <a href="/wiki/Ethnobotany" title="Ethnobotany">ethnobotany</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Museum Etnobotani</i></span>) was opened in 1982 and has more than 2000 exhibits;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etnobot_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-etnobot-108">[108]</a></sup> museum of the earth (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Museum Tanah</i></span>, 1988) represents hundreds of soil and rock samples from different parts of Indonesia;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zemlya_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-zemlya-109">[109]</a></sup> museum of the struggle (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Museum Perjuangan</i></span>, 1957) is devoted to the history of the Indonesian national liberation movement;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fighters_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-fighters-110">[110]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Pembela_Tanah_Air_Museum" title="Pembela Tanah Air Museum">Pembela Tanah Air Museum</a> (1996) reflects the history of the Indonesian military militia PETA (Pembela Tanah Air – "Defenders of the Motherland") created during World War II by the Japanese administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-predateli_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-predateli-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city has a drama theater,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teater_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-teater-112">[112]</a></sup> dozens of movie theaters, nine of which (as of mid-2010) are set up at international standards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kino_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-kino-113">[113]</a></sup> The presidential palace, administrative buildings and universities regularly host art exhibitions, and there are regular festivals of folk art, conferences and culture-related seminars, such as the Congress of Indonesian culture (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Kongres Kebudayaan Indonesia</i></span>) of 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KKI_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-KKI-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first hospitals were established in Bogor in the first half of the 19th century by the Dutch authorities. By the early 20th century, there were several civilian hospitals, a military hospital,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RS_Lama_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-RS_Lama-115">[115]</a></sup> and a large psychiatric hospital with doctors from Europe and North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nuthouse_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-nuthouse-116">[116]</a></sup> In the 1930s, the Dutch Red Cross Society hospital became the largest in the city. Most of the existing hospitals and clinics are built in the 1980s–1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rumah_Sakit_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rumah_Sakit-117">[117]</a></sup> They include 10 hospitals, 373 private clinics, 51 single-doctor clinics and 134 pharmacies and drug stores, and employ 274 general practitioners, 122 dentists, 74 sanitation doctors, 37 radiologists (X-ray), 141 gynaecologists, 32 nutritionists, 55 assistants, 710 nurses, 63 pharmacists and 99 doctors of other specialties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistika_51-6"><a href="#cite_note-Statistika-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rumah_Sakit_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rumah_Sakit-117">[117]</a></sup> 2 new hospitals are founded in 2014</p>
<p>The 12 hospitals of Bogor are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Hospital of the Indonesian Red Cross Society (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Rumah Sakit Palang Merah Indonesia</i></span>) – general, the oldest in the city</li>
<li>General Hospital of Bogor City (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Rumah Sakit Umum Daerah Kota Bogor</i></span>) – general, owned by the city government, formerly Karya Bhakti <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></li>
<li>Salak (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Rumah Sakit Salak</i></span>) – general, owned by the Indonesian Army</li>
<li>Atang Sanjaya (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Rumah Sakit TNI AU Atang Sanjaya</i></span>) – general, owned by the Indonesian Air Force, located in airbase area</li>
<li>Bogor Medical Centre – general practitioners, private</li>
<li>Islamic Hospital (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Rumah Sakit Islam</i></span>) – general</li>
<li>Azra (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Rumah Sakit Azra</i></span>) – general</li>
<li>Melania (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Rumah Sakit Melania</i></span>) – women and children</li>
<li>Hermina (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Rumah Sakit Hermina</i></span>) – women and children</li>
<li>Marzuki Mahdi (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Rumah Sakit Marzuki Mahdi</i></span>) – infectious diseases and psychiatric hospital</li>
<li>Mulia (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Rumah Sakit Mulia</i></span>)- general</li>
<li>Vania (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Rumah Sakit Vania</i></span>)- general, founded in Nov 1st, 2014 <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></li>
</ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bogor has three daily Indonesian-language newspapers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Koran_Daerah_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Koran_Daerah-120">[120]</a></sup> – "Radar Bogor", founded in 1998 and "Pakuan Raya" in founded in 2005 and Jurnal Bogor, founded in 2008. they print in about 25,000 copies and have electronic versions. Bogor offices also partly print part some Javanese and national newspapers. There are a few magazines and scientific publications of the local universities.</p>
<p>The two municipal TV channels, "Bogor-TV" and "Megasvara TV" broadcast at UHF channel 25 over the city and nearby areas of West Java.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TV_Daerah_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-TV_Daerah-121">[121]</a></sup> There are also at least 30 local radio stations, of which 20 are in the <a href="/wiki/Frequency_modulation" title="Frequency modulation">FM</a> and 10 in the <a href="/wiki/Amplitude_modulation" title="Amplitude modulation">AM</a> range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Radio_Bogor_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Radio_Bogor-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As of March 2010, the Bogor teams were registered in 28 sports to participate in national and regional competitions conducted by the <a href="/wiki/National_Sports_Committee_of_Indonesia" title="National Sports Committee of Indonesia">National Sports Committee of Indonesia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Komite Nasional Olahraga Indonesia</i></span>). Their achievements are regarded as poor. At the Java competitions, Bogor athletes took 5 gold medals instead of the planned 42.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42_medali_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-42_medali-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5_medali_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-5_medali-124">[124]</a></sup> The largest among 15 sports organizations<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistika_51-7"><a href="#cite_note-Statistika-51">[51]</a></sup> is the Bogor Football Union (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <span lang="id"><i>Persatuan Sepakbola Bogor</i></span>), headed by the current Mayor Diani Budiarto. The local football team "PSB Bogor" never took prizes in the national championships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sepak_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-sepak-125">[125]</a></sup> The local Stadium Pajajaran can accommodate 25,000 spectators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WS_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-WS-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Travel_and_places">Travel and places</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Travel and places">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bogor_Botanic_Gardens_lily_pond.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="531" data-file-width="800" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/Bogor_Botanic_Gardens_lily_pond.jpg/220px-Bogor_Botanic_Gardens_lily_pond.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/Bogor_Botanic_Gardens_lily_pond.jpg/330px-Bogor_Botanic_Gardens_lily_pond.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/Bogor_Botanic_Gardens_lily_pond.jpg/440px-Bogor_Botanic_Gardens_lily_pond.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bogor_Botanic_Gardens_lily_pond.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lily pond in the Bogor Botanical Garden.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On a national tourism exhibition of 2010 in Jakarta, Bogor was recognized as the most attractive tourist city of Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_best_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_best-127">[127]</a></sup> The city and its surrounding area are visited by about 1.8 million people per year, of whom more than 60,000 are foreigners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jumlah_wisatawan_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-jumlah_wisatawan-128">[128]</a></sup> The main tourist attraction is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bogor_Botanical_Garden" title="Bogor Botanical Garden">Bogor Botanical Garden</a>. Founded in 1817, it contains more than 6,000 species of tropical plants. Besides, about 42 bird species breed within the garden, although this number is declining and was 62 before 1952.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> The garden's 87-hectare area within the city was supplemented in 1866 by a 120-hectare park in suburban town of Cibodas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KRB_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-KRB-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o818_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-o818-131">[131]</a></sup> Much of the original rainforest was preserved within the garden providing specimens for scientific studes. Besides, the garden was enriched by collections of palms, bamboos, cacti, orchids and ornamental trees. It became famous in the late 19th century and was visited by naturalists from abroad to conduct scientific research. For example, the Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Petersburg_Academy_of_Sciences" title="St. Petersburg Academy of Sciences">St. Petersburg Academy of Sciences</a> had a Buitenzorg scholarship for young scientists to work at Bogor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KRB_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-KRB-130">[130]</a></sup> The staff of Bogor garden also administer three other major gardens of Iindonesia: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kebun_Raya_Cibodas" title="Kebun Raya Cibodas">Cibodas Botanical Garden</a> founded 1862 in West Java, the Purwodadi Botanical Garden in East Java and the <a href="/wiki/Bali_Botanic_Garden" title="Bali Botanic Garden">Bali Botanic Garden</a> founded in 1959 on <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a> island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brit_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-brit-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Istana_Bogor_side.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1712" data-file-width="2288" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Istana_Bogor_side.jpg/220px-Istana_Bogor_side.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Istana_Bogor_side.jpg/330px-Istana_Bogor_side.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Istana_Bogor_side.jpg/440px-Istana_Bogor_side.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Istana_Bogor_side.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The former residence of the Governor-General, now the summer palace of the President of Indonesia</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rooms-katholieke_kerk_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60016616.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="565" height="273" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rooms-katholieke_kerk_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60016616.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rooms-katholieke_kerk_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60016616.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rooms-katholieke_kerk_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60016616.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rooms-katholieke_kerk_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60016616.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rooms-katholieke_kerk_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60016616.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rooms-katholieke_kerk_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60016616.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Rooms-katholieke_kerk_Buitenzorg_TMnr_60016616.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cathedral. Photo 1920</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Another tourist attraction is the presidential palace with the total area of 28 hectares, including 1.8492 hectares of the palace buildings. The palace is surrounded by a park with a small pond.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KRB_130-2"><a href="#cite_note-KRB-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o817_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-o817-133">[133]</a></sup> The park is home to a herd of tame deer and is open to the public most of the year. The palace is accessible during holidays, such as the City Day and Independence Day; it has a collection of 450 paintings and 360 sculptures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KRB_130-3"><a href="#cite_note-KRB-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city and its suburbs contain dozens of medieval stone <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stelae" title="Stelae">stelae</a> (prasasti). Fifteen prasasti of the greatest historical and cultural value are collected in a special pavilion in the district of Batutulis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o827_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-o827-134">[134]</a></sup> In the western part of Bogor there is a large lake Gede (area 6 hectares) surrounded by the reserved forest area and a forest park. In the protected area there are several research facilities, and the recreation areas host sports activities, boating and fishing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Situ_Gede_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Situ_Gede-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o823_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-o823-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the territory of the botanic garden, there is a cemetery established in 1784.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ingat_Belanda_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ingat_Belanda-137">[137]</a></sup> It contains 42 historical graves of the Dutch colonial officials, military officers and scientists, who served in Bogor, Jakarta and other cities in West Java from the late 18th to early 20th centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ingat_Belanda_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ingat_Belanda-137">[137]</a></sup> Nearby, there are three graves of the early Sunda Kingdom (15th century): the wife of the founder of Bogor Silivangi, Galuh Mangku Alam, <a href="/wiki/Vizier" title="Vizier">vizier</a> Ba'ul and commander Japra. The locals regard these individuals as the city's patrons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Galuh_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Galuh-138">[138]</a></sup> Other historical places are the Bogor Cathedral – built in 1750, it is one of the oldest operational Catholic Churches in Indonesia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-o807_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-o807-139">[139]</a></sup> and the Buddhist temple Hok Tek Bio, built in 1672 in the classical South Chinese style. It is the first Buddhist temple of Bogor and one of the oldest in Indonesia.</p>
<p>Nearby is the <a href="/wiki/Jaksa_Waterfall" title="Jaksa Waterfall">Jaksa Waterfall</a>.</p>
<p>Recently Bogor launched new bus that can accommodate 25 passengers and this bus special to look around outside of Bogor Botanical Garden. Bus will be started from Botanical Square and ended up at the same place. This bus was unveiled by major of Bogor Bima Arya in 1 January 2017. This bus called UNCAL which means "Unforgattable City Tour at Lovable City".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Famous_people_born_in_Bogor">Famous people born in Bogor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Famous people born in Bogor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The list includes only people with Wikipedia pages in at least three languages.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adriaan_Fokker" title="Adriaan Fokker">Adriaan Fokker</a> (1887–1972) – Dutch physicist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hein_ter_Poorten" title="Hein ter Poorten">Hein ter Poorten</a> (1887–1968) – Commander of the armed forces of the Dutch East Indies in the early second World War II</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ru_den_Hamer" title="Ru den Hamer">Ru den Hamer</a> (1917–1988) – Dutch Olympic <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a> player</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ayu_Utami" title="Ayu Utami">Ayu Utami</a> (b. 1968) – Indonesian writer</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rudi_Soedjarwo" title="Rudi Soedjarwo">Rudi Soedjarwo</a> (b. 1971) – Indonesian playwright</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Suzzanna" title="Suzzanna">Suzzanna</a> (1942–2008) – Indonesian actress</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dr._Syed_Muhammad_Naq%C5%ABib_al-A%E1%B9%AD%E1%B9%ADas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dr. Syed Muhammad Naqūib al-Aṭṭas (page does not exist)">Dr. Syed Muhammad Naqūib al-Aṭṭas</a> (5 September 1931–) Muslim scholar</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei"><img alt="Brunei" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1440" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Brunei.svg/23px-Flag_of_Brunei.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Brunei.svg/35px-Flag_of_Brunei.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Brunei.svg/46px-Flag_of_Brunei.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Lumapas,_Brunei-Muara" title="Lumapas, Brunei-Muara">Lumapas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brunei_Darussalam" title="Brunei Darussalam">Brunei Darussalam</a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Indonesia" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Indonesia">List of twin towns and sister cities in Indonesia</a></li>
</ul>
